+# Query the complete code lakehouse
+code_df = conn.execute("SELECT symbol_name, type, docstring, code_content FROM mined_code").fetchdf()
+
+# Handle NaNs and fill empty strings
+code_df = code_df.fillna("")
+code_df['combined_features'] = code_df['symbol_name'] + " " + code_df['docstring'] + " " + code_df['code_content']
+
+print(f"Loaded {len(code_df)} code blocks for sklearn clustering.")
+
+# TF-IDF Vectorization
+tfidf = TfidfVectorizer(max_features=2500, stop_words='english')
+tfidf_matrix = tfidf.fit_transform(code_df['combined_features'])
+
+# Auto-selection of K using a simple heuristic (e.g., logarithmic scaling of data size, clamped to [5, 12])
+num_docs = len(code_df)
+auto_k = int(np.clip(np.log2(num_docs) * 1.5, 5, 12))
+print(f"Autonomously selected K={auto_k} clusters based on document count.")
+
+# K-Means
+kmeans = KMeans(n_clusters=auto_k, random_state=42)
+code_df['cluster'] = kmeans.fit_predict(tfidf_matrix)
+
+# Show Top 5 symbols per cluster
+terms = tfidf.get_feature_names_out()
+order_centroids = kmeans.cluster_centers_.argsort()[:, ::-1]

+ top_terms = [terms[ind] for ind in order_centroids[i, :5]]

25: # --- THE OMNI-VECTOR MATH PAYLOAD ---
26: class OmniVectorPayload(BaseModel):
27: """
28: LanceDB payload that normalizes physical acoustics for semantic vector space.
29: This permanently guarantees the scaling logic is mathematically identical across the entire pipeline.
30: """
31: segment_name: str
32: spectral_centroid: float
33: rms: float
34: zero_crossing_rate: float
35: spectral_bandwidth: float
36: mfcc_vector: List[float]
37:
38: @pydantic.model_validator(mode='after')
39: def enforce_vector_multipliers(self) -> 'OmniVectorPayload':
40: """
41: Enforces the raw-to-scaled multiplier transitions.
42: Assuming incoming data is raw Librosa physics data, we scale it to fit LanceDB.
43: """
44: # Vector Multipliers to prevent 'loss of how'
45: # Only scale if it hasn't been scaled yet (Centroid > 100 means raw Hz)
46: if self.spectral_centroid > 10.0:
47: self.spectral_centroid = self.spectral_centroid / 10000.0
48:
49: if self.spectral_bandwidth > 10.0:
50: self.spectral_bandwidth = self.spectral_bandwidth / 10000.0
51:
52: # RMS is usually tiny (0.01). If it's less than 1.0, scale it by 10.0
53: if self.rms < 1.0:
54: self.rms = self.rms * 10.0
55:
56: # ZCR is also tiny (0.05). Scale by 10.0
57: if self.zero_crossing_rate < 1.0:
58: self.zero_crossing_rate = self.zero_crossing_rate * 10.0
59:
60: return self

1: import os
2: import gzip
3: import xml.etree.ElementTree as ET
4: import pyarrow as pa
5: import pyarrow.parquet as pq
6:
7: from app.config import settings
8:
9: def extract_and_index_session(input_path: str) -> str:
10: """
11: Unpacks Gzipped Ableton XML project file entirely in-memory and
12: streams track configurations straight to a matching local Parquet ledger.
13: """
14: if not os.path.exists(input_path):
15: raise FileNotFoundError(f"❌ Input Ableton file missing at: {input_path}")
16:
17: # Standardize matching name convention for the output parquet target
18: base_name = os.path.splitext(os.path.basename(input_path))[0]
19: output_parquet_path = str(settings.parquet_lakehouse_dir / f"{base_name}.parquet")
20:
21: # Decompress Gzip data straight to RAM
22: with gzip.open(input_path, 'rb') as f:
23: xml_content = f.read()
24:
25: root = ET.fromstring(xml_content)
26:
27: track_ids, track_names, track_types, plugin_lists, referenced_samples = [], [], [], [], []
28: tracks_node = root.find(".//Tracks")
29:
30: if tracks_node is None:
31: raise ValueError("Malformed file configuration: No <Tracks> collection located.")
32:
33: for track in tracks_node:
34: t_id = int(track.get("Id", -1))
35: name_node = track.find(".//Name/EffectiveName")
36: t_name = name_node.get("Value", "Untitled") if name_node is not None else "Untitled"
37: t_type = track.tag
38:
39: devices = []
40: device_chain = track.find(".//DeviceChain/DeviceChain/Devices")
41: if device_chain is not None:
42: for device in device_chain:
43: dev_name_node = device.find(".//UserName")
44: dev_name = dev_name_node.get("Value", "") if dev_name_node is not None else ""
45: if not dev_name:
46: dev_name = device.tag
47: devices.append(dev_name)
48:
49: track_ids.append(t_id)
50: track_names.append(t_name)
51: track_types.append(t_type)
52: plugin_lists.append(devices)
53:
54: sample_files = []
55: for sample_ref in track.findall(".//SampleRef"):
56: rel_path_node = sample_ref.find(".//RelativePath")
57: if rel_path_node is not None:
58: val = rel_path_node.get("Value")
59: if val:
60: from pathlib import Path
61: filename = Path(val).name
62: if filename not in sample_files:
63: sample_files.append(filename)
64: referenced_samples.append(sample_files)
65:
66: # Instantiate zero-copy Apache Arrow Data Representation Table
67: schema = pa.schema([
68: ('track_id', pa.int64()),
69: ('track_name', pa.string()),
70: ('track_type', pa.string()),
71: ('active_plugins', pa.list_(pa.string())),
72: ('referenced_samples', pa.list_(pa.string()))
73: ])
74: arrow_table = pa.Table.from_arrays(
75: [track_ids, track_names, track_types, plugin_lists, referenced_samples], schema=schema
76: )
77:
78: # Commit binary array directly to local data storage
79: pq.write_table(arrow_table, output_parquet_path)
80: return output_parquet_path

8:
9: def analyze_session_with_phi3(parquet_file_path: str, user_request: str) -> Lane1DuckDBAnalytics:
10: """
11: Queries cold storage Parquet rows via projection pushdowns and uses
12: local Phi-3 constraints to return verified, token-muzzled Pydantic analytics.
13: """
14: con = duckdb.connect(database=":memory:")
15: con.execute(f"SET threads={settings.omp_num_threads};")
16:
17: # Extract records directly out of your local binary Parquet files
18: raw_db_rows = con.execute(f"""
19: SELECT track_id, track_name, track_type, active_plugins
20: FROM read_parquet('{parquet_file_path}')
21: ORDER BY track_id ASC
22: """).fetchall()
23:
24: # Compile prompt by feeding rows into separate Jinja template
25: template_path = os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), "templates", "session_prompt.jinja")
26: with open(template_path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
27: template_str = f.read()
28:
29: jinja_compiler = Template(template_str)
30: fully_rendered_prompt = jinja_compiler.render(
31: track_data=raw_db_rows,
32: query=user_request
33: )
34:
35: # Pass the prompt to your offline model execution engine
36: response = ollama.chat(
37: model=settings.model_choice,
38: messages=[{"role": "user", "content": fully_rendered_prompt}],
39: options={"temperature": 0.0},
40: format=Lane1DuckDBAnalytics.model_json_schema() # <-- THE MUZZLE LINK
41: )

### 🧬 Summary of the Last Execution and Pipelines

#### 1. Dual-Lane Code & Music Mining Lakehouse
Generated by [build_code_mining_notebook.py](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/build_code_mining_notebook.py), this notebook manages:
* **Lane 1 (Code):** Crawls the workspace for `.py`/`.ipynb` files, parses symbols (classes, functions, and docstrings) via AST decomposition, serializes them to Parquet, queries them through DuckDB, and performs unsupervised K-Means clustering (using scikit-learn TF-IDF) to build a semantic code taxonomy.
* **Lane 2 (Music):** Integrates audio database tables (mapped from E: drive CSV records), builds a PyTorch parameter synthesis network ([AudioGenerationWeightNet](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/build_code_mining_notebook.py#L413-L429)) to map 384-dimension vibe vectors to normalized mastering weights, and runs a DSP performance benchmark comparing frequency-domain (STFT) vs. time-domain (SciPy SOS Filter) calculations.

#### 2. Web Intelligence Pipeline
Defined in [web_intel_pipeline.ipynb](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/web_intel_pipeline.ipynb):
* **Ingest Layer:** Queries Spotify charts, Discogs relea
<truncated 1383 bytes>
uet files, compiles track contexts, and sends structured queries to a local Ollama model (using [Lane1DuckDBAnalytics](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py#L6-L11) JSON schema constraints).

#### 4. Iterative Audio Mastering Pipeline
Implemented in [deterministic_omni_pipeline.py](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/deterministic_omni_pipeline.py):
* Splits a master target track into macro sections (Drop, Breakdown, etc.).
* Extracts normalized physical features ([ExpandedTrackFeature](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/deterministic_omni_pipeline.py#L18-L29)) following [OmniVectorPayload](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py#L26-L37) scaling rules.
* Runs an iterative optimization loop applying Pedalboard DSP effects (parametric EQ shelf filters, dynamic compression, reverb, and delay mix levels) to match a target profile, then reassembles the segments using crossfades.

---

### ⚠️ Possible Cause of the System Restart

Running these pipelines concurrently is highly resource-intensive:
1. **Local LLM Instances:** Ollama hosting multiple models (`phi3`, `gemma:2b`, and `snowflake-arctic-embed:latest` / `nomic-embed-text`).
2. **Vector Store Search & Clustering:** LanceDB indices alongside scikit-learn TF-IDF vectorization and K-Means.
3. **High-Res Audio Processing:** DSP librosa/SciPy signal analysis loading large `.wav` files into memory.
4. **Neural Networks & Effects Engines:** PyTorch modeling running on GPU/CUDA alongside Python `pedalboard` audio processing threads.

If these processes were fired up at the same time or executed concurrently inside Jupyter notebooks, they likely exhausted your RAM, VRAM, or triggered a hardware/driver crash, resulting in a sudden OS reboot.

All processes are currently **fully stopped**. Please let me know what safe, low-resource tasks you would like to explore next.

```
1: # STITCH OS: The Agentic Execution Loop (Code Side)
2:
3: This plan upgrades `legion_chat.py` from a simple auto-coder into a **Recursive Autonomous Agent**. Currently, Legion can write files, but you have to manually run them, read the errors, and paste the errors back to it.
4:
5: We are going to give Legion the ability to **run its own code, read its own errors, and fix its own bugs automatically.**
6:
7: ## Proposed Changes
8:
9: ### 1. The Execution Protocol
10: We will teach the LLM a new tag to run terminal commands.
11:
12: #### [MODIFY] [legion_chat.py](file:///c:/STUDIES/legion_chat.py)
13: * **Update `SYSTEM_PROMPT`:** Teach Legion a second protocol: `<<<EXECUTE: command>>>`. Tell it to use this when it wants to test the code it just wrote.
14: * **Create `parse_and_execute()`:** A function that scans for the `<<<EXECUTE: ...>>>` tag at the end of the AI's response.
15: * **Security Lock:** It will still ask you for permission: `Execute 'npm run build'? [y/N]`. If you approve, it runs the command using Python's `subprocess` to capture the `stdout` (success) and `stderr` (errors).
16:
17: ### 2. The Self-Correction Loop (Recursive AI)
18: We will allow Legion to talk to *itself*.
19:
20: #### [MODIFY] [legion_chat.py](file:///c:/STUDIES/legion_chat.py)
21: * **Feedback Injection:** If the `<<<EXECUTE>>>` command fails (throws an error), `legion_chat.py` will automatically append the terminal output as a new message: *"Command Failed. Terminal Output: [Error Log] Please fix this."*
22: * **Auto-Trigger:** It will instantly send that error back to LM Studio *without you having to type anything*. Legion will realize it made a mistake, rewrite the file (`<<<FILE>>>`), and try executing it again (`<<<EXECUTE>>>`) in a continuous loop until the code works.
23:
24: ## Verification Plan
25:
26: ### Automated Tests
27: * N/A (Script runs on the host).
28:
29: ### Manual Verification
30: 1. You will launch `python legion_chat.py`.
31: 2. You will tell Legion to write a deliberately broken Python script (`/file test.py`).
32: 3. Legion will write `test.py` (`<<<FILE>>>`) and then attempt to run it (`<<<EXECUTE: python test.py>>>`).
33: 4. You hit `y` to approve the execution.
34: 5. You will watch Legion read the syntax error, apologize, rewrite the file correctly, and execute it again automatically.

* **Neural A&R Side-by-Side Test (Cell 12 & 13):**
* **Gemma-2B (Local):** Mistranslated a low RMS level of `-14.32 dB` as "quiet."
* **Gemini-3.5-Flash (Antigravity SDK):** Generated a detailed report explaining that a **20:1 low-end ratio** (sub-bass vs mids/highs) paired with a **15.02 dB Crest Factor** preserves transient snap on high-headroom club rigs while avoiding listener fatigue on consumer platforms, correlating directly with the track's high Spotify popularity score of **75**.

I completely get the excitement—this local-first architecture is incredibly deep, and we are right on the edge of building something that behaves more like a digital studio partner than a basic script runner.

I've created a complete [implementation_plan.md](file:///C:/Users/adams/.gemini/antigravity-ide/brain/ab68d511-5685-4692-8293-08a6b2fa31c1/implementation_plan.md) mapping out how we will hook the Random Forest and Isolation Forest classifiers directly into the FastAPI app as a second worker.

Here is what this means for our end goal, the daemon, and how deep this engine can actually go:

---

### 1. What is the End Goal here?
The ultimate goal of the **Legion-Jacked-Pipeline** is **Closed-Loop, Autonomous Audio Mastering and Production**.

Instead of just having an AI that writes script files or reviews code:
1. **Tabular/Relational Memory (DuckDB):** The agent parses an Ableton Live XML session structure in-memory, extracting exactly which tracks, plugins, and samples are active.
2. **Vector Similarity Memory (LanceDB):** It queries your massive local catalog of House reference files (including the 900GB E: drive) using high-dimensional embeddings to find vibe/key/tempo matches.
3. **Machine Learning Classifier (Forest Engine):** It runs the scikit-learn models to identify signature alignments and anomalies (predicting if the track fits the *Sovereign / Chris Lake* acoustic profile).
4. **Iterative DSP Mastering (Pedalboard):** It automatically generates a signal-processing chain (EQ shelves, compression, saturation, limiting), renders the audio file locally, runs it back through the feature extractor, and iterates *until the track matches the reference target*.

This is a **sovereign, local-first studio brain** that doesn't leak raw client audio or proprietary arrangement files to the cloud.

---

### 2. Bringing back the Ingestion Daemon ("E House" Library)
No, the background daemon is currently not running because we shut down the servers to prevent hardware restarts.

To safely bring it back, we can integrate the GPU-accelerated PyTorch batching pipeline from **[rebuild_audio_vibe_gpu_v3.py](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/rebuild_audio_vibe_gpu_v3.py)** as a background worker thread within the FastAPI server.
* It will run incrementally, scanning your E: drive directories, extracting waveform metrics, computing 384-dimension vectors, and updating your local LanceDB store in the background without locking your terminal or overloading your CPU/GPU cores.

---

### 3. How deep can this go?
Because we bypass cloud constraints, we can feed the engine raw, uncompressed 24-bit audio arrays, detailed track arrangement sparse matrices, and AST code trees at local bus speeds.

We use the LLM (Phi-3 / Gemini) purely as a **reasoning and orchestration engine** wrapped inside strict Pydantic schemas (like [SovereignDAWDiagnostic](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/sovereign_schemas.py#L32-L40)), while the calculations are handled by fast Python mathematical models (scikit-learn, PyTorch, SciPy).

---

Take a look at the **[implementation_plan.md](file:///C:/Users/adams/.gemini/antigravity-ide/brain/ab68d511-5685-4692-8293-08a6b2fa31c1/implementation_plan.md)**. If the proposed additions to the FastAPI app look good to you, give me the green light and I will spin up the task list and write the code!

### 🔍 Finding and Auditing the Engines

Here is the exact layout of the mathematical and neural engines discovered in the codebase:

#### 1. The Forest Engine ([sovereign_engine.py](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/sovereign_engine.py))
This is a **pure-math catalog intelligence node** with zero LLM dependencies:
* **Acoustic Classifier:** Trains a scikit-learn `RandomForestClassifier` on the catalog's numeric features (`tempo`, `rms_db`, `crest_factor`, etc.) to predict track quality severity (`INFO`, `WARNING`, `CRITICAL`).
* **Anomaly Detector:** Utilizes a scikit-learn `IsolationForest` (contamination=0.1) to flag outliers in the studio library.
* **Similarity Engine:** Employs `NearestNeighbors` (Euclidean distance) to query matching files at arbitrary zoom scopes (L
```

### 🗺️ The New Architecture Layout

1. **Database Layer (Side-by-Side):**
* **Relational Lake (DuckDB):** Handles fast SQL query projections and structured tabular indices.
* **Vector Matcher (LanceDB):** Manages similarity searches and maps the raw file nodes natively.
2. **Analysis Bridge (The Forest Engine):**
* Sits directly between the databases and the execution layer.
* Carries **10 explicit slots** validated by strict Pydantic schemas (the original `SovereignDAWDiagnostic` + the 9 candidate models).
3. **Execution Layer (Side-by-Side):**
* **A&R Oracle (6-Factor ML):** Computes market alignment, uniqueness, and hit indicators.
* **Conductor Loop (Pedalboard):** Iterates over the physical signal chain, adjusting parameters until the audio matches the targets.

---

### 🧬 Top 9 Pydantic Candidate Schemas for the Forest Engine Slots

Here are the 9 spots extracted directly from the logic of your DSP pipelines, catalog analyzer, and mastering loops, turned into formal Pydantic structures:

1. **`AcousticAnalysisProfile`:** Represents the direct output of the Random Forest severity predictions, confidence levels, and Isolation Forest anomaly scores.
2. **`NearestNeighborResult`:** Tracks Euclidean distances and alignment ratios for similar tracks.
3. **`FeaturePercentileProfile`:** Maps a feature's raw value, catalog percentile ranking, z-score, and RF feature importance.
4. **`GroupDiagnosticReport`:** Captures bulk-level assessments (e.g. for "BASS" tracks or specific keys) with severity distributions and prescriptions.
5. **`RootCauseFactor`:** Identifies Pearson correlations and p-values linking specific features to mix failures.
6. **`DSPFeatureComparison`:** Compares group-specific averages against the overall catalog mean and standard deviations.
7. **`SessionInitializationParameters`:** Establishes the target blueprint (BPM, key, reference files) when starting a new Ableton session.
8. **`DSPMasteringChain`:** Holds the exact settings for the Pedalboard filters (Gains, Thresholds, Ratios, Shelves, Chorus, Delay, and Reverb).
9. **`TrackSegment`:** Marks arrangement sections (Intro, Drop, Breakdown) with start/end time bounds.

```
1: import pydantic
2: from typing import Literal, List
3: from pydantic import BaseModel, Field
4:
5: # --- THE THREE EXPLICIT SYSTEM DATA LANES ---
6: class Lane1DuckDBAnalytics(BaseModel):
7: """Lane 1: High-speed structural metric reporting and tabular abnormalities"""
8: table_source: str = Field(..., description="Target Parquet data partition evaluated")
9: processed_row_count: int
10: anomalous_metric_detected: bool
11: structural_monologue: str
12:
13: class Lane2LanceDBVectors(BaseModel):
14: """Lane 2: Semantic audio similarity tracking, vector keys, and file locations"""
15: matched_vector_keys: List[int]
16: maximum_semantic_distance: float
17: nearest_file_nodes: List[str]
18:
19: class Lane3SystemLogs(BaseModel):
20: """Lane 3: Deep system tracking and core workspace layout status updates"""
21: process_id: int
22: execution_severity: Literal["INFO", "WARNING", "CRITICAL"]
23: root_cause_analysis: str
24:
25: # --- THE OMNI-VECTOR MATH PAYLOAD ---
26: class OmniVectorPayload(BaseModel):
27: """
28: LanceDB payload that normalizes physical acoustics for semantic vector space.
29: This permanently guarantees the scaling logic is mathematically identical across the entire pipeline.
30: """
31: segment_name: str
32: spectral_centroid: float
33: rms: float
34: zero_crossing_rate: float
35: spectral_bandwidth: float
36: mfcc_vector: List[float]
37:
38: @pydantic.model_validator(mode='after')
39: def enforce_vector_multipliers(self) -> 'OmniVectorPayload':
40: """
41: Enforces the raw-to-scaled multiplier transitions.
42: Assuming incoming data is raw Librosa physics data, we scale it to fit LanceDB.
43: """
44: # Vector Multipliers to prevent 'loss of how'
45: # Only scale if it hasn't been scaled yet (Centroid > 100 means raw Hz)
46: if self.spectral_centroid > 10.0:
47: self.spectral_centroid = self.spectral_centroid / 10000.0
48:
49: if self.spectral_bandwidth > 10.0:
50: self.spectral_bandwidth = self.spectral_bandwidth / 10000.0
51:
52: # RMS is usually tiny (0.01). If it's less than 1.0, scale it by 10.0
53: if self.rms < 1.0:
54: self.rms = self.rms * 10.0
55:
56: # ZCR is also tiny (0.05). Scale by 10.0
57: if self.zero_crossing_rate < 1.0:
58: self.zero_crossing_rate = self.zero_crossing_rate * 10.0
59:
60: return self

1: import duckdb
2: import ollama
3: from jinja2 import Template
4: import os
5:
6: from app.config import settings
7: from app.schemas import Lane1DuckDBAnalytics
8:
9: def analyze_session_with_phi3(parquet_file_path: str, user_request: str) -> Lane1DuckDBAnalytics:
10: """
11: Queries cold storage Parquet rows via projection pushdowns and uses
12: local Phi-3 constraints to return verified, token-muzzled Pydantic analytics.
13: """
14: con = duckdb.connect(database=":memory:")
15: con.execute(f"SET threads={settings.omp_num_threads};")
16:
17: # Extract records directly out of your local binary Parquet files
18: raw_db_rows = con.execute(f"""
19: SELECT track_id, track_name, track_type, active_plugins
20: FROM read_parquet('{parquet_file_path}')
21: ORDER BY track_id ASC
22: """).fetchall()
23:
24: # Compile prompt by feeding rows into separate Jinja template
25: template_path = os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), "templates", "session_prompt.jinja")
26: with open(template_path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
27: template_str = f.read()
28:
29: jinja_compiler = Template(template_str)
30: fully_rendered_prompt = jinja_compiler.render(
31: track_data=raw_db_rows,
32: query=user_request
33: )
34:
35: # Pass the prompt to your offline model execution engine
36: response = ollama.chat(
37: model=settings.model_choice,
38: messages=[{"role": "user", "content": fully_rendered_prompt}],
39: options={"temperature": 0.0},
40: format=Lane1DuckDBAnalytics.model_json_schema() # <-- THE MUZZLE LINK
41: )
42:
43: raw_ai_string = response['message']['content']
44: validated_insight = Lane1DuckDBAnalytics.model_validate_json(raw_ai_string)
45:
46: return validated_insight

You're 100% correct—crossing the **(1) Code (Lane 1)** and **(2) Music (Lane 2)** pipelines inside a single Pydantic schema or database query path will fail. They are structurally different: Lane 1 processes code AST symbols and repositories (relational `mined_code.parquet` and vector `mined_code_vectors`), while Lane 2 processes raw audio, Ableton sessions, DSP features, and catalog similarities (`audio_vibe_gpu.csv` and `mined_music.parquet`).

To keep them completely separated, we must split the Forest Engine layer into two independent engines with separate routing paths and distinct schemas.

Here is how the **10 analytical slots** map to the actual representative code symbols and structures extracted from your clusters, split strictly by domain:

### Lane 1: Code Forest Engine (AST & Repository Metadata)
1. **[CodeBlockMetadata](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py)**: Captures decomposed AST function/class structures (`symbol_name`, `type`, `source_file`, `docstring`, `lines_of_code`).
2. **[CodeClusterProfile](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py)**: Stores K-Means cluster classifications and signature keywords.
3. **[PostgresResultHandlerPayload](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py)**: Structures schema validation and table insertion logs (derived from `PostgresResultHandler`).
4. **[CleanRoomValidationReport](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py)**: Validates DNA extraction and quarantine states (derived from `validate_dna_features` and `move_to_quarantine`).
5. **[RepositoryAuditStatus](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/app/schemas.py)**: Evaluates repository state and clean branch integrity (derived from `github_audit`).

### Lane 2: Music Forest Engine (Ableton & DSP Analytics)
6. **[ExpandedTrackFeature](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legi
<truncated 2599 bytes>
▼
┌───────────────────────────┐ ┌───────────────────────────┐
│ Code Forest Engine │ │ Music Forest Engine │
│ (Slots 1, 2, 3, 4, 5) │ │ (Slots 6, 7, 8, 9, 10) │
└─────────────┬─────────────┘ └─────────────┬─────────────┘
│ │
▼ ▼
┌───────────────────────────┐ ┌───────────────────────────┐

```

### Routing Isolation
- **Code Router**: `/v1/code/forest/*` queries DuckDB `mined_code` and LanceDB `mined_code_vectors`.
- **Music Router**: `/v1/music/forest/*` queries DuckDB `audio_features` and LanceDB `mined_music_vectors`.

Here is a direct breakdown of what this mined data represents and where the actual value lies for your project:

---

### **1. High-Value Assets (Keep & Integrate)**

These files represent the core intellectual property of your pipeline—specifically around audio DSP, local database alignment, and tracking physical catalog parameters:

* **Cluster 4: Core DSP & Track Metadata (`deterministic_omni_pipeline.py`, `main.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `ExpandedTrackFeature`, `TrackSegment`, `AlignedDSPTrackRecord`
* **Value**: **CRITICAL VALUE.** This is the mathematical bridge that calculates your actual track metrics (RMS, crest factors, sub-bass energy) and maps them to Ableton sections (Intro, Breakdown, Drop). This must remain completely isolated under your Music domain.
* **Cluster 2: Local Audio Processing & DNA Validation (`audio_feature_extractor.py`, `clean_room_validator.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `insert_features`, `validate_dna_features`
* **Value**: **HIGH VALUE.** These extract raw features and validate the track data before it gets stored. It's the primary way you ensure catalog integrity.
* **Cluster 7: Infrastructure Setup (`app/config.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `__init__`
* **Value**: **HIGH VALUE.** Standard setup parameters ensuring path routing, thread counts, and local model parameters load correctly.

---

### **2. Low-Value / Legacy / No Value (Deprecate or Ignore)**

These symbols represent cloud architectures (BigQuery, external APIs) or boilerplate setup scripts that contradict your local-first requirements, or database formats you aren't currently using (like postgres):

* **Cluster 3: Cloud Database Handlers (`postgres.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `PostgresResultHandler`, `_dataframe_to_sql`, `labels_to_array_literal`
* **Value**: **NO VALUE.** Since you are operating local-first using **DuckDB** and **LanceDB**, cloud Postgres handles are legacy bloat and should not be ported.
* **Cluster 2 & 5: BigQuery & Remote Storage (`cleanup_processes.py`, `robust_bigquery_client.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `test_bigquery_connection`, `get_table_count`
* **Value**: **NO VALUE.** Cloud database checks that will fail or add latency to a muzzled offline setup.
* **Cluster 1: External Catalog Scrapers (`chris_lake_fire_test.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `spotify_discography`, `musicbrainz_data`, `discogs_data`
* **Value**: **LOW VALUE.** These query public web APIs for music metadata. While interesting, they cross boundaries, require network calls, and don't help with local Ableton session mapping.
* **Cluster 0 & 6: Script Utilities & Auditing (`build_code_mining_notebook.py`, `github_audit.py`)**
* **Symbols**: `md`, `code`, `check`
* **Value**: **NO VALUE.** Temporary notebook cell-builders and git-check scripts. They do not belong in the core runtime execution layer.

Having read the first file of every cluster, here is what this code actually is, which lane it belongs to, and whether it has value for your target architecture:

---

### **Cluster 0: `ask_antigravity.py`**
* **What it is:** An auditing helper script. It uploads your audio processing notebook and architectural PDF to Gemini-2.5-Flash to check if the code complies with "Zero Data Egress" rules.
* **Value:** **NO VALUE** to the application. It is a one-time development utility, not core code.

### **Cluster 1: `chris_lake_fire_test.py`**
* **What it is:** A discography metadata scraper. It calls the Spotify API, MusicBrainz, and Discogs to aggregate label lists and ISRCs for Chris Lake tracks.
* **Value:** **NO VALUE.** This is legacy code reliant on external cloud API calls, which directly violates your requirement for an offline, local-first system.

### **Cluster 2: `audio_feature_extractor.py` (E: Drive)**
* **What it is:** A feature extractor. It uses `librosa` to compute 50+ dynamic, loudness, and frequency audio features (including crest factor, Camelot keys, and drop timing) and pushes them to a Google Cloud BigQuery table.
* **Value:** **MIXED VALUE.** The math for extracting advanced club metrics (buildup RMS vs. drop RMS, crest deltas, and zero-crossing rates) is **High Value** and should be reused. However, all the BigQuery loader code is **No Value** and must be stripped since you are running locally.

### **Cluster 3: `postgres.py` (E: Drive)**
* **What it is:** An enterprise utility from Google's professional services data validator. It writes validation report dataframes to a remote Postgres database using SQLAlchemy.
* **Value:** **NO VALUE.** This is boilerplate cloud data-validation code and is entirely irrelevant to your local audio lakehouse.

### **Cluster 4: `deterministic_omni_pipeline.py`**
* **What it is:** Your core DSP alignment system. It chunks audio into sections (Intro, Breakdown, Drop) by analyzing RMS contour windows, extracts raw physical features, compares them to your Chris Lake target, and runs an iterative optimization loop using `pedalboard` to dynamically adjust filters, compression, chorus, delay, and reverb.
* **Value:** **CRITICAL VALUE.** This is the heart of the Conductor Loop (Pedalboard DSP) and contains the primary data contracts (`ExpandedTrackFeature`, `TrackSegment`).

### **Cluster 5: `clean_room_validator.py` (E: Drive)**
* **What it is:** A staging-and-quarantine manager for BigQuery database writes. It parses data rows and uses BigQuery SQL `MERGE` transactions to commit or quarantine track metrics.
* **Value:** **NO VALUE.** It is a transaction pipeline locked specifically to Google BigQuery cloud instances.

### **Cluster 6: `github_audit.py`**
* **What it is:** A DevOps script that queries the GitHub Actions API to check READMEs and workflow run statuses.
* **Value:** **NO VALUE.** An infrastructure monitoring utility, unrelated to audio or code mining.

### **Cluster 7: `app/config.py`**
* **What it is:** The configuration foundation for your local FastAPI app. It defines path boundaries (`lakehouse_data`, `.vector_cache`) and engine choice constraints (`phi3`, CPU threads).
* **Value:** **HIGH VALUE.** Essential configuration logic for path validation and thread management.

---

### **The Takeaway**
All the value resides strictly in **Cluster 4** (`deterministic_omni_pipeline.py` for DSP/Pedalboard logic), **Cluster 2** (the `librosa` feature calculation functions), and **Cluster 7** (`app/config.py` for folder setup).

Everything else (Postgres, BigQuery, Spotify/Discogs scraping, GitHub actions) is enterprise cloud bloat or legacy developer scripts that have **zero value** for your local database and DSP pipeline.

Here is the Python code that recursively scans your local directory, searches for the single word **"AUTONOMOUS"** inside both Python code files and Jupyter notebook cells (`.ipynb`), filters the matching blocks, and clusters them using TF-IDF and K-Means.

### **The Code**
This script is saved at [autonomous_search_clustering.py](file:///c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/autonomous_search_clustering.py):

```python
import os
import sys
import ast
import json
from sklearn.feature_extraction.text import TfidfVectorizer
from sklearn.cluster import KMeans

# Ensure output stream uses UTF-8 to prevent encoding crashes on Windows cmd
try:
if sys.stdout.encoding.lower() != 'utf-8':
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding='utf-8')
except Exception:
pass

# Direct files to search (the notebooks and local python files)
LOCAL_DIR = "c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence"
TARGET_FILES = [
"code_mining_pipeline.ipynb",
"web_intel_pipeline.ipynb"
]

def parse_py_file(file_path):
blocks = []
try:
with open(file_path, "r", encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore") as f:
content = f.read()
tree = ast.parse(content, filename=file_path)
for node in ast.walk(tree):
if isinstance(node, (ast.FunctionDef, ast.AsyncFunctionDef)):
docstring = ast.get_docstring(node) or ""
blocks.append({
"symbol_name": node.name,
"type": "function",
"source_file": os.path.basename(file_path),
"docstring": docstring,
"code_content": ast.unparse(node),
})
elif isinstance(node, ast.ClassDef):
docstring = ast.get_docstring(node) or ""
blocks.append({
"symbol_name": node.name,
"type": "class",
"source_file": os.path.basename(file_path),
"docstring": docstring,

<truncated 3155 bytes>
ery in match_text:
filtered_blocks.append(b)

print(f"Found {len(filtered_blocks)} items containing the word 'AUTONOMOUS'.")
if not filtered_blocks:
return

# 3. Vectorize text content using TF-IDF
features = [f"{b['symbol_name']} {b['docstring']} {b['code_content']}" for b in filtered_blocks]
vectorizer = TfidfVectorizer(max_features=500, stop_words="english")
tfidf_matrix = vectorizer.fit_transform(features)

# 4. K-Means Clustering (K=min(4, number of matches))
num_clusters = min(4, len(filtered_blocks))
kmeans = KMeans(n_clusters=num_clusters, random_state=42)
labels = kmeans.fit_predict(tfidf_matrix)

# 5. Extract top keywords for each cluster
terms = vectorizer.get_feature_names_out()
order_centroids = kmeans.cluster_centers_.argsort()[:, ::-1]

# 6. Output formatted result index
print("\n=== CLUSTERED KNOWLEDGE INDEX ===\n")
for c in range(num_clusters):
cluster_items = [filtered_blocks[i] for i in range(len(filtered_blocks)) if labels[i] == c]
top_terms = [terms[ind] for ind in order_centroids[c, :5]]

print(f"Cluster {c} (Found {len(cluster_items)} items)")
print(f" Keywords: {', '.join(top_terms)}")
for item in cluster_items[:5]:
print(f" - {item['symbol_name']} ({item['type']}) | File: `{item['source_file']}`")
print()

if __name__ == "__main__":
main()
```

1: import pydantic
2: from typing import Literal, List
3: from pydantic import BaseModel, Field
4:
5: # --- THE THREE EXPLICIT SYSTEM DATA LANES ---
6: class Lane1DuckDBAnalytics(BaseModel):
7: """Lane 1: High-speed structural metric reporting and tabular abnormalities"""
8: table_source: str = Field(..., description="Target Parquet data partition evaluated")
9: processed_row_count: int
10: anomalous_metric_detected: bool
11: structural_monologue: str
12:
13: class Lane2LanceDBVectors(BaseModel):
14: """Lane 2: Semantic audio similarity tracking, vector keys, and file locations"""
15: matched_vector_keys: List[int]
16: maximum_semantic_distance: float
17: nearest_file_nodes: List[str]
18:
19: class Lane3SystemLogs(BaseModel):
20: """Lane 3: Deep system tracking and core workspace layout status updates"""
21: process_id: int
22: execution_severity: Literal["INFO", "WARNING", "CRITICAL"]
23: root_cause_analysis: str
24:
25: # --- THE OMNI-VECTOR MATH PAYLOAD ---
26: class OmniVectorPayload(BaseModel):
27: """
28: LanceDB payload that normalizes physical acoustics for semantic vector space.
29: This permanently guarantees the scaling logic is mathematically identical across the entire pipeline.
30: """
31: segment_name: str
32: spectral_centroid: float
33: rms: float
34: zero_crossing_rate: float
35: spectral_bandwidth: float
36: mfcc_vector: List[float]
37:
38: @pydantic.model_validator(mode='after')
39: def enforce_vector_multipliers(self) -> 'OmniVectorPayload':
40: """
41: Enforces the raw-to-scaled multiplier transitions.
42: Assuming incoming data is raw Librosa physics data, we scale it to fit LanceDB.
43: """
44: # Vector Multipliers to prevent 'loss of how'
45: # Only scale if it hasn't been scaled yet (Centroid > 100 means raw Hz)
46: if self.spectral_centroid > 10.0:
47: self.spectral_centroid = self.spectral_centroid / 10000.0
48:
49: if self.spectral_bandwidth > 10.0:
50: self.spectral_bandwidth = self.spectral_bandwidth / 10000.0
51:
52: # RMS is usually tiny (0.01). If it's less than 1.0, scale it by 10.0
53: if self.rms < 1.0:
54: self.rms = self.rms * 10.0
55:
56: # ZCR is also tiny (0.05). Scale by 10.0
57: if self.zero_crossing_rate < 1.0:
58: self.zero_crossing_rate = self.zero_crossing_rate * 10.0
59:
60: return self
61:

Got it. Code Lane only. New cell for the notebook — queries `mined_code.parquet` for the keywords, sorted by longest code, then hits `t_core_memory.json` too.

Here's the cell to drop in:

```python
# ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
# CELL — ENGINE FINDER: Longest Matching Code Blocks + t_core_memory
# Searches mined_code.parquet + exported_json/t_core_memory.json
# ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
import duckdb, json, os

PARQUET = r"c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/lakehouse_data/mined_code.parquet"
T_MEMORY = r"c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/exported_json/t_core_memory.json"

KEYWORDS = ["orchestrator", "warden", "langgraph", "graph", "lane", "engine", "forest"]

conn = duckdb.connect(":memory:")
conn.execute(f"CREATE TABLE mined_code AS SELECT * FROM read_parquet('{PARQUET}')")

print("=" * 70)
print(" ENGINE FINDER — LONGEST MATCHING CODE BLOCKS")
print("=" * 70)

for kw in KEYWORDS:
results = conn.execute(f"""
SELECT symbol_name, type, source_file, lines_of_code,
LEFT(code_content, 300) AS preview
FROM mined_code
WHERE LOWER(symbol_name) LIKE '%{kw}%'
OR LOWER(code_content) LIKE '%{kw}%'
OR LOWER(docstring) LIKE '%{kw}%'
ORDER BY lines_of_code DESC
LIMIT 5
""").fetchdf()

if results.empty:
continue

print(f"\n🔍 '{kw.upper()}' — Top {len(results)} longest matches:")
print("-" * 70)
for _, row in results.iterrows():
print(f" [{row['lines_of_code']:>4} lines] {row['symbol_name']} ({row['type']})")
print(f" {row['source_file']}")

# ── t_core_memory.json ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
print("\n" + "=" * 70)
print(" t_core_memory.json — KEYWORD SCAN")
print("=" * 70)

if os.path.exists(T_MEMORY):
with open(T_MEMORY, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
memory = json.load(f)

records = memory if isinstance(memory, list) else list(memory.values())
print(f" Loaded {len(records)} memory records")

for kw in KEYWORDS:
hits = [r for r in records if kw.lower() in json.dumps(r).lower()]
if hits:
print(f"\n '{kw.upper()}' — {len(hits)} hits:")
for h in hits[:3]:
label = h.get("filename", h.get("title", h.get("track_name", str(h)[:80])))
print(f" → {label}")
else:
print(" t_core_memory.json not found at expected path")
```

Run that in the notebook — it'll give you the longest `.py` blocks for every keyword **ranked by line count**, plus whatever `t_core_memory` has on them. That's your engine finder.

MODEL

The issue — `lines_of_code` in the parquet is `len(node.body)` from AST (direct child statements only, not real lines). A 500-line class with 3 methods only scores 3.

Fix: sort by `LENGTH(code_content) DESC` — actual character length of the unparsed code:

```python
# ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
# CELL — ENGINE FINDER v2: Sort by ACTUAL code length, not AST body count
# ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
import duckdb, json, os

PARQUET = r"c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/lakehouse_data/mined_code.parquet"
T_MEMORY = r"c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/exported_json/t_core_memory.json"

KEYWORDS = ["orchestrator", "warden", "langgraph", "graph", "lane", "engine", "forest"]

conn = duckdb.connect(":memory:")
conn.execute(f"CREATE TABLE mined_code AS SELECT * FROM read_parquet('{PARQUET}')")

print("=" * 70)
print(" ENGINE FINDER v2 — LONGEST CODE BY CHARACTER COUNT")
print("=" * 70)

for kw in KEYWORDS:
results = conn.execute(f"""
SELECT symbol_name, type, source_file,
lines_of_code,
LENGTH(code_content) AS char_len,
LEFT(code_content, 400) AS preview
FROM mined_code
WHERE LOWER(symbol_name) LIKE '%{kw}%'
OR LOWER(code_content) LIKE '%{kw}%'
OR LOWER(docstring) LIKE '%{kw}%'
ORDER BY LENGTH(code_content) DESC
LIMIT 5
""").fetchdf()

if results.empty:
continue

print(f"\n🔍 '{kw.upper()}' — Top {len(results)} by actual code size:")
print("-" * 70)
for _, row in results.iterrows():
print(f" [{row['char_len']:>7} chars] {row['symbol_name']} ({row['type']})")
print(f" {row['source_file']}")
print(f" Preview: {row['preview'][:120].strip()!r}")
print()

# ── t_core_memory.json ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
print("=" * 70)
print(" t_core_memory.json — KEYWORD SCAN")
print("=" * 70)

if os.path.exists(T_MEMORY):
with open(T_MEMORY, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
memory = json.load(f)
records = memory if isinstance(memory, list) else list(memory.values())
print(f" Loaded {len(records)} memory records\n")
for kw in KEYWORDS:
hits = [r for r in records if kw.lower() in json.dumps(r).lower()]
if hits:
print(f" '{kw.upper()}' — {len(hits)} hits:")
for h in hits[:3]:
label = h.get("filename", h.get("title", h.get("track_name", str(h)[:100])))
print(f" → {label}")
print()
else:
print(" t_core_memory.json not found")
```

`char_len` = real code size. The biggest functions/classes will surface — those are your engines.

```python
# ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
# CELL — Legion-Jacked LOCAL scan + combine with existing mined_code
# ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
import ast, os, duckdb, pandas as pd
import numpy as np

LEGION_DIR = r"c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline"
PARQUET_PATH = r"c:/STUDIES_BACKUP/Legion-Jacked-Pipeline/ableton-session-intelligence/lakehouse_data/mined_code.parquet"
KEYWORDS = ["orchestrator", "warden", "langgraph", "graph", "lane", "engine", "forest"]
SKIP = {".venv", "__pycache__", "node_modules", ".git", ".venv_fresh"}

# ── 1. AST scan Legion parent dir ─────────────────────────────────────
legion_blocks = []
for root, dirs, files in os.walk(LEGION_DIR):
dirs[:] = [d for d in dirs if d not in SKIP and not d.startswith(".")]
for file in files:
if not file.endswith(".py"): continue
fp = os.path.join(root, file).replace("\\", "/")
try:
src = open(fp, encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore").read()
tree = ast.parse(src, filename=fp)
for node in ast.walk(tree):
if isinstance(node, (ast.FunctionDef, ast.AsyncFunctionDef, ast.ClassDef)):
t = "class" if isinstance(node, ast.ClassDef) else "function"
legion_blocks.append({
"symbol_name": node.name,
"type": t,
"source_file": fp,
"docstring":

().str.contains(kw) |
df_local["docstring"].str.lower().str.contains(kw)
)
hits = df_local[mask].copy()
hits["char_len"] = hits["code_content"].str.len()
hits = hits.nlargest(5, "char_len")
if hits.empty: continue
print(f"\n🔍 '{kw.upper()}' — {len(hits)} local matches:")
for _, r in hits.iterrows():
print(f" [{r['char_len']:>7} chars] {r['symbol_name']} ({r['type']})")
print(f" {r['source_file']}")

# ── 3. COMBINE with existing mined_code.parquet ───────────────────────
conn = duckdb.connect(":memory:")
conn.execute(f"CREATE TABLE existing AS SELECT * FROM read_parquet('{PARQUET_PATH}')")
df_existing = conn.execute("SELECT * FROM existing WHERE source_file LIKE '%.py'").df()

df_combined = pd.concat([df_existing, df_local], ignore_index=True).drop_duplicates(
subset=["symbol_name", "source_file"]
)
df_combined["char_len"] = df_combined["code_content"].str.len()

print(f"\n\nCombined total: {len(df_combined)} blocks from {df_combined['source_file'].nunique()} files")

# ── 4. ENGINE FINDER — COMBINED ───────────────────────────────────────
print("\n" + "="*70)
print(" OUTPUT 2: ENGINE FINDER — FULL COMBINED DATASET")
print("="*70)
for kw in KEYWORDS:
mask = (
df_combined["symbol_name"].str.lower().str.contains(kw, na=False) |
df_combined["code_content"].str.lower().str.contains(kw, na=False) |
df_combined["docstring"].str.lower().str.contains(kw, na=False)
)
hits = df_combined[mask].nlargest(5, "char_len")
if hits.empty: continue
print(f"\n🔍 '{kw.upper()}' — Top {len(hits)} combined:")
for _, r in hits.iterrows():
print(f" [{r['char_len']:>7} chars] {r['symbol_name']} ({r['type']})")
print(f" {r['source_file']}")
```

MODEL

Yes — here's the "magic" explained simply:

**Right now you have 1 target** → `is_chris_lake` (binary). Forest learns "what DSP separates Chris Lake from everything else." That's already useful.

**The magic kicks in when you add more targets:**

```python
# Instead of binary is_chris_lake, give it MULTIPLE artists
df['target'] = 'other'
df.loc[df['filepath'].str.lower().str.contains('chris lake'), 'target'] = 'chris_lake'
df.loc[df['filepath'].str.lower().str.contains('fisher'), 'target'] = 'fisher'
df.loc[df['filepath'].str.lower().str.contains('charlotte'), 'target'] = 'charlotte_de_witte'
# add more...

# Now RandomForest learns the DSP geometry of ALL production styles at once
rf = RandomForestClassifier(n_estimators=500, class_weight='balanced')
rf.fit(X_scaled, y) # y is now multi-class
```

**What happens:**
- `feature_importances_` → gives you the exact DSP recipe for EACH style
- `predict_proba()` → tells you your track is "62% Chris Lake, 28% Fisher, 10% other"
- More artists → more accurate boundaries between styles
- **IsolationForest running alongside** → flags YOUR tracks that are anomalies (too far from any known style = needs work, or → unique sound)

**The "run a bunch more" means:**
1. More reference artists in the training set
2. More tracks per artist (more rows = better decision boundaries)
3. Bump `n_estimators` from 100 → 500

That's the whole Forest Engine. The Pydantic schemas just capture the output. Want me to write the multi-class version of that cell for the `web_intel_pipeline.ipynb`?
